Commercial News

Financial: Gold Market Fluctuated Last Week

▲The Future Holds More Drastic Changes

▲A Summary of the Entire Week: Last week, the gold market formed a swirling pattern, with changeable conditions and frequent fluctuations. Foreign news was mixed. At the beginning of the week, it was above 740 taels. Subsequently, due to the drop in silver prices, it suddenly broke through the 50-tael mark. However, the London Conference, with the German President ordering the minting of 500 million marks in silver currency and 100 million marks in copper currency to alleviate the financial crisis, caused panic. The price of gold almost collapsed, plummeting by 20 taels to 732 taels, before hovering around 40 taels. The total fluctuation for the week was 23 taels and 2 mace, with a net increase of only 2.5 taels. As the British and American silver markets remained unchanged, the Shanghai exchange rate also did not experience any special gains or losses. Some gold businesses made net purchases of British gold, while the Dalian group sold Dalian drafts, all in hedging transactions. Market transactions varied. The Dalian group remained long, while the Guangdong group remained on the sidelines, without any activity. Speculators' transactions differed greatly. The daily exchange rate was around 40-50 taels. The spot market was sluggish, leading to a decline in prices. Current inventories are quite high. The future of the gold market is likely to undergo another drastic change, depending on the stability of Germany's finances. The following is a summary of the week's developments:

▲Daily Fluctuations: From Monday (July 20), the large-scale exchange rate rose by 1.25, and the silver price also rose by 1.25, but the prior order remained unchanged. The domestic market seemed loose. The initial opening of the September gold market fell by 4 taels to 743 taels, followed by 2.5 taels. Subsequently, buying increased, pushing it up to 48 taels and 4 mace. However, sellers were also active, causing it to fall to 43 taels. It then recovered, with unstable fluctuations. It retreated from 47 taels to 44-45 taels. In the afternoon, large players unloaded, and the market closed at 43 taels and 3 mace, a further decrease of 3 taels and 7 mace from the previous Saturday. Transaction volumes of various firms were not high, and the market situation was relatively stable. The next day, the large-scale exchange rate remained unchanged, the silver price rose by another 1.25, and the exchange market was stable. The gold market opened at 44 taels and 7 mace, an increase of 1 tael and 4 mace. Speculators bought at 47 taels, which increased to 49 taels at noon. The market closed at 7 taels and 6 mace, with the Dalian group selling. In the afternoon, it reached 3 taels and 2 mace and closed at 4 taels and 7 mace, a rebound of 1 tael and 4 mace compared to the previous day. The overall situation for the day remained unchanged, with a fluctuation of only 5 taels and 8 mace. On Wednesday, the large-scale silver exchange rate decreased by 1.25, and the silver price decreased slightly by 0.25, but the prior order remained the same. Businesses tried to sell gold for profits. The gold market opened at 51 taels and 5 mace, a rise of 6 taels and 8 mace, followed by 54 taels and 5 mace. There were more buyers than usual. Soon, a Mr. Wu sold, breaking through the 50-tael mark. At noon, it was 48 taels, 1 mace, and 2 cents. In the afternoon, it initially stabilized and then fell to 45 taels and 5 mace, before slightly improving to 7 taels and 5 mace. It closed at 6 taels and 2 mace, an increase of 1 mace and 5 cents compared to the previous day. There was a difference of 9 taels throughout the day. On Thursday, the large-scale exchange rate remained unchanged, the silver price decreased by 1.25, and the prior order remained unchanged. The domestic market suddenly loosened. Businesses bought and sold repeatedly. The gold market was closed in the morning due to mourning for the overseas Chinese, but trading continued in the black market, with prices ranging from 51.5 taels to 55 taels, and then back to 51 taels, with uneven transactions. In the afternoon, the formal market reopened as usual at 54 taels and 5 mace, followed by 5 taels and 2 cents. The reason for the rise was the independent decrease in silver prices, the fall in New York stocks, and the small decline in the Indian exchange rate, leading to a strong market sentiment. Moreover, sellers were active, and rumors arose, such as the assassination of Finance Minister Song and the rumor that Germany would mint silver coins to circulate in the market, requiring the purchase of silver blocks. This news caused panic, leading to a sharp drop in prices by more than 20 taels, plummeting to 32 taels. Businesses such as the large player Mr. Wu and a certain Japanese merchant tended to sell. Later, it recovered, with shorts taking advantage to buy in, reaching over 40 taels. The market closed at 39 taels and 5 mace, still down 6 taels and 7 mace. The difference in half a day was as much as 23 taels and 2 mace, making it difficult to predict. The next day, the large-scale exchange rate decreased by 0.0625, the silver price decreased slightly by 0.125, and the prior order was as usual. The domestic market was stable. The gold market opened at 44 taels and 5 mace, a rise of 5 taels. It then went from 47 taels and 5 mace to 35 taels and 1 mace, before rising again to 45 taels. This was due to the uncertainty, with large players entering and exiting the market, causing prices to fluctuate. The market closed at 40 taels at noon. The afternoon was stable, with fluctuations of only 2-3 taels. The market closed at 3 taels and 5 mace, an increase of 4 taels. The difference between the high and low prices was 12 taels and 4 mace. Most firms tended to sell. On Saturday, the large-scale silver exchange rate increased by 0.0625, the silver price also increased by 0.125, and the prior order remained unchanged. The domestic market was tight. The gold market continued to rise, opening at 44 taels and 5 mace, followed by 6 taels and 5 mace to 3 taels. At 10:30 AM, the news suddenly broke that India was selling silver, causing panic. Speculators such as Mr. Lu competed to buy, leading to a sharp rise of 6 taels to 50 taels. Sellers continued to sell, and the exchange rate remained stable, with banks willing to sell, pushing it further to 47 taels and 8 mace. The market closed at 49 taels and 5 mace, an increase of 6 taels. However, the black market closed at 46 taels due to unloading by Hengyu Fuchang and others. The difference in half a day was 7 taels. Securities: Bond Market Quiet Last Week

▲Trends Stagnant, with Slight Fluctuations Compared to the Previous Week

In the past week, the bond market in Shanghai was quiet. Spot transactions were increasingly rare, with only 24,900 yuan traded throughout the week. Among them, demobilization bonds accounted for 10,900 yuan, with the rest being extremely scarce. The futures market was also calm, with daily transactions quite slow. Except for the first day of the week, which reached over 19 million yuan, the remaining days were mostly around 14 million yuan. On Thursday, there was only one afternoon trading session, with only over 6 million yuan traded. The total transaction volume for the week was 81.98 million yuan, less than the previous week by 38.3 million yuan. Among them, 20-year customs bonds accounted for the most, at 28.59 million yuan. Other bonds included 20-year cigarette bonds at 13.79 million yuan, 19-year customs bonds at 10.53 million yuan, 19-year good deeds bonds at 9.73 million yuan, demobilization treasury bonds at 6.465 million yuan, 96 public bonds at 2.42 million yuan, consolidation 6% bonds at 1.36 million yuan, customs treasury bonds at 1.055 million yuan, and financial and 7-year bonds each at 5,000 yuan. In addition, unified tax treasury bonds were gradually traded at 100,500 yuan. Finally, spot transactions for Shanghai Bank shares, which were newly opened for auction, amounted to 20 shares.

Regarding the fluctuations in bond prices last week, the situation was very dull, as described below. The situation showed little improvement. The Guangdong issue remained unresolved, the northern Shi army revolted again, and the end of the anti-communist campaign was still pending. Market sentiment was weak, and large players were waiting and watching. Supply and demand were balanced, but bond prices felt somewhat stagnant, with slight daily fluctuations. On Monday, most bonds rose by 0.8-0.9 yuan to 1.7-1.8 yuan. On Tuesday, they fell back, with 9 customs bonds and 20 customs bonds each down by a small 0.8-0.9 yuan. On Wednesday, they turned firm, with 20 customs bonds improving by about 1 yuan and others also improving by about half a yuan. On Thursday, they returned to weakness, but only by a small number of corners. On Friday, the decline was stronger, with 19 good deeds bonds and 20 customs bonds down by 0.6-0.7 yuan to over 1 yuan. The weekend was also weak and stagnant. The trend was chaotic throughout. The results showed mixed gains and losses compared to the previous week, with the numbers being very small. Judging from the trend, it seems difficult to have large gains or losses before settlement. The stock exchange has decided to cancel the seller's provision of physical goods for the August term starting next week and instead collect a margin of 2,000 yuan. However, for the September futures that have not yet been auctioned, selling is still limited to providing physical goods. Yarn & Cotton: Yarn Sales Very Active Last Week

▲Fine Yarn Insufficient Supply

▲Yarn Auction Price Increased by Over Two Taels

The yarn market was exceptionally strong at the beginning of the past week. As the inspection of inferior goods became increasingly strict, native yarn became stronger. The price of 42-count fine yarn soared by more than 20 taels in one day due to a shortage of goods, which was insufficient to meet the demand. Various groups resumed purchasing to rush production, causing the daily line to jump suddenly. The prices of 16-count and 20-count native yarn gradually increased, and spot goods became increasingly scarce. As for the customers, in view of the heated atmosphere of the boycott, the masses purchased non-stop for the sake of preventing future troubles, so spot transactions became more and more enthusiastic. The market trend was up without falling, and the auction price of yarn also rose accordingly. The spot market was tight, and more and more buyers purchased, and before long overseas yarn and cotton conditions tended to fall, a war broke out in the north, and the market slightly fell again. As a result, prices for each month were over two taels higher than the previous week. The total transaction volume for the week was 226,250 packages, with the most purchases from the mainland, Guangdong, and Sichuan groups. Judging from the general trend, the yarn market is still in a stable situation, but the incessant rains and increasingly serious reports of floods in various places have generally made people nervous, anticipating that autumn sales will be greatly affected. Cotton Prices Rose by About One Taels Last Week

▲Benefited by the Ink Rain

The cotton market was very quiet at the beginning of the week. Because overseas cotton market was weak and gold prices were also hovering, and local cotton factories had no need, transactions were completely cut off, so people were particularly uneasy, and the market was in a big downturn. Before long, it rained continuously. At the same time, cotton in Hubei and Shaanxi was damaged by floods, resulting in greater losses. The local market was stimulated by the replenishment of empty orders. Subsequently, the city was heavily rained, the floods in various places had become more intense, so the mainland groups came to Shanghai to purchase one after another, and the rising trend turned sharp. However, the Huoji group and the Shanghai group were throwing it all out consistently, while Indian and American cotton fell again, the oppression was still heavy, so the rising trend was still level. However, looking back to the floods in the country, the cotton production had been severely hit, and the future of the cotton market was unimaginable. The prices of cotton in each month were about one or two taels higher than the previous week, spot transactions were deserted, and the source was 2,210 bales of Yao cotton, and 557,500 dan of cotton had been transacted and graded by marks. Youth Garden

Sailor's Spirit

— Wang Bingqian

After the school bell rang, the four of us returned to the room one after another. Each of us seemed a little unhappy because the final exam was approaching for us who usually played from morning till night, and we still didn't understand the lessons.

"Alas, time flies so fast. The big exam is the day after tomorrow," Zhu sighed.

"It's all my fault. I made so much noise every day that you couldn't study," Xiu said, shedding tears.

"That unlucky beard, the textbook will cover more than sixty pages. And that old Li thing, we have to hand in the arithmetic practice book tomorrow," Shu said anxiously, because people who do a lot of arithmetic practice questions make six or seven notebooks, and those who do less have two or three notebooks, but she doesn't even have half a notebook.

"I'm going to do arithmetic," Shu said, taking a handful of books, as well as an ink bottle, eraser, and many other things to the reading room.

So Zhu sat at the table reading, Xiu was reciting English on the bed, and I was copying notes, which suddenly broke our room's record for studying hard.

"Hey, hey," Shu said, holding a newspaper in one hand and a large bag of peanuts in the other, excitedly jumping in, "Look, Carlton is doing 'Sailor's Spirit.' Let's go watch it, okay?"

"Seconded," I said, pressing the copy, "Who's in the mood to copy? Let's go quickly, it's 5:15. Zhu, Xiu, what about you?"

"Stop pretending," Shu threw Zhu's chemistry to the ground.

"I can't go," Xiu was indeed studying seriously.

"Today is our last day of leisure," I said, "After this, we'll be scattered everywhere. Where else will we have the opportunity to get together? Don't spoil people's fun."

"But how can we get out of the school gate? It would be terrible if Old Fox saw us," Zhu said.

"It doesn't matter, just sneak out one by one," Shu said, looking at me with a smile.

"Okay, okay, but Zhu, don't dress up too seductively. It won't be fun if we get caught," I warned her.

"Humph, you're the one who attracts attention, with your two little braids,"

In five minutes, we had everything ready. We sneaked to the tram stop one by one. With great difficulty, we got on the tram.

"Look, look, Mr. Zhang," Xiu shouted. We all looked in the direction she was pointing. It was indeed Mr. Zhang sitting in the front third-class car, tilting his head and looking outside. The four of us lowered our heads. I was especially afraid of being seen with my two little braids. We hid in horror beside Shu, not daring to talk or laugh, just looking anxiously at our destination. We jumped off the car and walked quickly to Carlton.

"Ah, what if we meet the teachers in the movie theater? That would be terrible," I said timidly.

"We're already here, can't turn back," Shu said, "I think the teachers are all stingy. Who would be willing to spend one dollar for a ticket?" I nodded in agreement, so we all bought tickets and went in.

The inside was already crowded with many spectators. We chose to sit in the very back, talking and laughing freely.

"Not good, Mr. He, Mr. Zhao, Mr. Lai, over there, over there,"

Shu exclaimed.

We saw those three sitting in the sixth row right in front of us.

"What should we do?" I asked anxiously.

"Quick, lower your heads, don't let them see you," Xiu ordered.

"They're looking back," Shu was peeking at their movements.

Zhu held my cold hand tightly. I felt her trembling.

"It won't matter after the show starts," Xiu still had some ideas.

The whole place was dark. The Metro newsreel and the slapstick film were over. "Sailor's Spirit" was on the screen.

"We have to go out before the show ends, otherwise they will definitely see us," I suggested. They all agreed.

"Zhu, don't be afraid," Shu also realized that Zhu was terribly scared.

"What—what will happen if—if they see—see us," Zhu sobbed.

"Let's just go now," Xiu knew that we were in no mood to watch the show anymore.

Before 6 o'clock, we rushed back to school.

What a regret. We spent four dollars, didn't watch the show, and ended up with a scare. We were extremely upset.

Before and After Graduation

— Wan

(1)

Xian was a "Bachelor" graduating from the Department of Political Science of the Faculty of Law this year. Before graduation, everyone called him County Magistrate, — some even jokingly called him the County Magistrate of Haimen County — because Xian was big and looked majestic, with an appearance (?) that really resembled a county magistrate. Xian himself was happy to accept this "County Magistrate" title, and he seemed to have no intention of taking any job other than County Magistrate after graduation.

It has been more than a month and a half since graduation, and Xian has sent express letters and registered letters to relatives and friends... so far, there is no certainty. Not to mention County Magistrate, even a clerical worker in a government office or a teacher in a primary or secondary school, earning forty or fifty yuan a month, is still unattainable, making the big guy restless.

Xian's only hope is to beg the head of the Department of Political Science to find a position in the Municipal Education Bureau. Xian said to his department head, "No matter what I do, it's fine,..." but he still often says to others, "Within ten years, I will eventually become a county magistrate. The fortune teller said that I will have official luck within two years, at twenty-seven and twenty-eight years old..."

(2)

Mo was a "Bachelor" graduating from the Faculty of Education this year. He was very active in school, served as the chairman of the student council, and was quite close to the vice-president... He often told people that his only way out after graduation depended on the vice-president's recommendation.

It has been more than a month and a half since graduation, and there is still no news about a position for the fall. During summer school, the vice-president also came to the school to work. Mo was afraid that it would be inconvenient to talk to the vice-president at school, so he simply went to his house.

He was afraid that he wouldn't be home during the day, so he would go at night. He would go at nine o'clock at night.

Mo went to the vice-president's house at nine o'clock the night before.

"Sir," Mo had just uttered "Sir," and before he could finish his sentence, a voice said "He's gone." The tone of voice seemed to contain an insulting meaning.

Mo looked in from outside the door. It was clear that the vice-president was inside, but as soon as he heard someone asking for him, he quickly turned around and went upstairs. In an instant, Mo had seen everything clearly.

(3)

Chun was a "Bachelor" graduating from the Faculty of Science this year. When he was about to graduate, he begged his advisor to find him a job. One day, he ran into his advisor.

"Sir, please find... because I..." Chun said tremblingly, unable to speak the words.

"Okay,..." the advisor agreed readily. Chun's joy was indescribable. Everything depended on the advisor.

One evening, Chun went to his advisor's house again to see the advisor, inquire about good news, and beg for everything.

"There may be a position in the rural normal school, I will pay attention," because the advisor also served as the director of the rural normal school.

Chun was happy, danced with joy, and took his leave.

The advisor resigned as the head of a certain department at this university and as the director of the rural normal school, and went to Nanjing Central Political School to teach, no longer in Shanghai. This news was already confirmed, but Chun has not yet received the advisor's good news.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions

(1) The text should be limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education,... are examples of introductions, but boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures should be limited to recent works by new artists at home and abroad and related illustrations related to the text.

Social News

Life of Career Women in New York (8)

— Lin

The following is the daily life of a woman who earns twenty to twenty-five dollars a week, Clarae Williams.

Her original name was Clara, which should be acknowledged. Many of the girls she knew had lovely and resonant names, so later she felt that it was more appropriate to use the name Clarae.

Clarae works as a cigar sales clerk in a large New York hotel. If she doesn't make any advances each month, she will have twenty-five dollars in her pay envelope at the end of the week. She works very late every day, so this drama of life always opens around ten o'clock in the morning. Clarae and a girl of her equal status live together. These women feel that living on Eighty Street West is still very good. Their rooms all have running water facilities.

Clarae's family lives in New Jersey, but she left home and went out several years ago. She feels ashamed of her family, although she still has some love for them. Her mother is too old-fashioned, and her father smokes a pipe all day long and doesn't care about anything else, especially about his nitpicking daughters. Clarae's first position was in a candy store outside Jersey City. She felt very satisfied, and the living environment was also acceptable. Later, she met a traveling salesman who told her that she was beautiful and could work as a salesgirl in a New York hotel, where they needed attractive women to fill this position in the lobby. At first, Clarae was not eager to realize this proposal. She had only been to the lobby of a large New York hotel once or twice in her life. She had a fear in her heart, afraid that someone would ask her what she was doing there. But this traveling salesman who made the proposal came to the city every week and always reiterated his previous proposal. Clarae asked him which hotel he was recommending, and he wrote her a list of hotels. It had also been several weeks since she decided to go to New York. One afternoon, she decided to leave and left her name at several hotels. One of them was hiring, but they wanted to meet other women first and then give her a reply. Clarae or Clara, as she was called at the time, was very surprised when she received a letter telling her to go to work on Monday. Her parents did not approve of this move very much. Clara was willing to continue living at home and going to New York to work every day. What pleased her parents was that her weekly salary had increased from twelve to eighteen dollars.

In three years, her salary increased to twenty-five dollars a week, and her job was still the same as before. She had left home, which surprised her parents greatly. Now she has become an old New Yorker.

On this particular morning, she lingered in bed and refused to get up immediately, but she had to be at the hotel by twelve o'clock, and she still had to wash a few shirts and socks. She also had to find her own breakfast, so she had to get up and light the "Sterno" to boil water and coffee. The coffee she used could be eaten after a little boiling. A can of milk, a piece of bread, a few pieces of butter, and some crackers were leftovers from last night and were placed on the small table to have for breakfast. Her roommate had already gone out to work.

After breakfast and laundry, Clarae began to get dressed. She carefully combed and dressed. First, she cleaned her face with powder, and then successively used glossy cream, rouge, dry powder, lipstick, eyebrow pencil, and other cosmetics. Finally, she applied a thin layer of fine powder on her face. She had to carefully examine her face. "Her face is like peach blossoms and cheese," many people praised her. She not only worked hard to put on makeup, but also spent a lot of money to maintain her color and make it flawless.

Time passed quickly. Clarae hurriedly made her bed and tidied up the room at the same time, otherwise she knew her roommate would be angry. However, she didn't care much about her roommate's affairs. In short, she would tidy up if she wanted to, otherwise she would just let it be.

She wore a tight-fitting fake leather short jacket, which was her favorite outfit. The hat she wore was also very tight and small, with a feather decoration that dragged straight down to her cheek. The high-heeled slippers and extremely thin socks completed her entire visible outfit.

Clarae likes to take the Fifth Avenue bus to work. The fare is one coin and change, which she feels is also very worthwhile. Taking the bus is more decent than taking the subway. She likes to imagine herself sitting in a private sedan, speeding all the way.

The hotel where Clarae works has a wide variety and large number of customers. Wealthy people from outside the city often stay in this hotel because it is very convenient to get to the large stores and theaters. Large merchants also regard this hotel as their headquarters, and store buyers from various cities and towns also gather here, coming and going very busy. (To be continued)

Strange Letters Recently Found in Society

— Ren Nongxuan

In the past two days, I have repeatedly received letters from my friend Mr. Jin Sheng Fan Ziying via mail. Upon reading them, I realized they were about a "Chain of Happiness," which was quite mysterious and deeply suspicious. According to the letter, within twenty-four hours, one must copy the letter nine times and forward it to various friends. It claims that doing so will bring the best fortune and happiness, and even a large fortune of 250 million yuan. Otherwise, an ominous omen will immediately follow. The claims are absurd and unbelievable, and I do not know where they originated. If true, friends in this city would need to spend nine cents on postage, and thirty-six cents for those in other cities, plus the cost of stationery, totaling at least four jiao (角, a unit of currency) of silver. One could say that the small fortune is lost before the large fortune arrives. I am publishing the original letter below to inform the readers of the newspaper, hoping to eliminate superstition.

Chain of Happiness

This chain can bring the best fortune and luck. It must be forwarded without interruption. If interrupted, misfortune will immediately follow. This chain was invented by a Colonel of the U.S. Army artillery during the European War. The intention was to wrap this chain around the Earth three times, which would have miraculous effects. Copy this chain nine times and send it to nine good friends you want to bring good luck to. Within nine days of sending, the sender will surely experience something extremely pleasant and satisfying. This has been tested and proven repeatedly. If someone receives this letter, they must forward it within twenty-four hours. For example, Mr. Weber followed the instructions and copied and sent the letter. On the ninth day after sending it, he won a prize of two million yuan. Mr. Li Te, however, did not pay attention to the chain and did not forward it, resulting in the collapse of his most magnificent house. There was also a Mrs. Hong in the Bai Si Qiao area who did not pay attention and did not forward or copy the letter, and her only son died within three days. Mr. Jia Shi Duan, on the other hand, believed in the chain and copied and forwarded it on time, and actually obtained a large fortune of 250 million yuan. Translated by 2.6132.

I, Ren Nongxuan, sent it to Huang Mingyi. Huang Mingyi sent it to Guan Zhuqing. Guan Zhuqing sent it to Xiang Juchuan. Xiang Juchuan sent it to Bai Ziliang. Bai Ziliang sent it to Lu Shaonan. Lu Shaonan sent it to Tang You Shi. Tang You Shi sent it to Di Yingxian. Di Yingxian sent it to Gao Zhong. Gao Zhong sent it to Hu Dieyun. Hu Dieyun sent it to Zhang Xiaolou. Zhang Xiaolou sent it to Jiang Zhuzhuang. Jiang Zhuzhuang sent it to Jin Songcen. Jin Songcen sent it to Yao Junxian. Yao Junxian sent it to Yan Jinsheng. Yan Jinsheng sent it to Ren Nongxuan. Please be sure to copy it nine times on time and send it to friends, that is essential.

U.S. Cotton Planting Area and Harvest Volume

41 million acres planted this year, with a harvest of 13 million bales expected.

According to the U.S. Department of Agriculture, as of the 1st of this month, the U.S. cotton planting area is 41,149,100 acres, a decrease of 9.95% compared to last year, close to the general prediction (a decrease of 11%). The planting area and actual harvest volume for the past five years are as follows (unit: thousands of acres, actual harvest volume in thousands of bales):

Planting Area Actual Harvest Volume

1931 41,491

1930 46,078 13,932

1929 47,067 14,825

1928 46,946 14,477

1927 41,905 12,956

1926 48,720 17,977

Furthermore, according to observations from some sources, due to the good cultivation conditions, the harvest volume this year is expected to reach 13 million bales.

German Goods Make Great Strides in the Eastern Market Again

Japan has a large trade deficit with Germany, and the market in China is also unstable in the future.

Tokyo News: The trade volume between Germany and Japan, according to the statistics of the recent five years, is as follows (unit: thousands of Japanese yen):

Japan's Exports to Germany Germany's Exports to Japan

1926 8,151 145,220

1927 10,612 131,390

1928 12,582 133,537

1929 13,446 157,273

1930 11,106 106,183

In addition, in the first five months of this year, Japan's total exports to Germany were worth 3,481,000 Japanese yen, and Germany's total exports to Japan were worth 39,813,000 Japanese yen. Japanese financial figures are quite worried about the increase in German goods imports. According to them, Germany has been selling its industrial products on the world market in recent years to alleviate its financial difficulties. As a result of the recent economic crisis, it is feared that its implementation of sales will become even more urgent. According to the above table, in the trade relationship between Japan and Germany, Japan is in a position of large trade deficit, losing a lot of money every year. German industrial products such as steel, rayon, and dyes have always been popular in China and other markets. After the European War, they were excluded by Japanese goods, but now the market for German goods is gradually recovering, and Japanese goods will inevitably decrease. Therefore, Japanese merchants are quite alarmed.

Marshal Foch's European War Diary

— Translated by Gu Angruo

At the Abbeville Conference on May 12, the Allied governments had already decided on the outline of transporting American troops to France in May and June.

The Allied governments again held a conference in Versailles on June 2, inviting Marquis Milner, Commander Pershing, and myself to propose a plan for transporting American troops in July. We then reached an agreement, acknowledging the prior transportation of infantry in June, and now advocating that July proceed according to the original plan. In July, 140,000 infantry and machine gun units must be sent to France.

The Supreme Military Council not only approved this agreement but also expressed its hope that the United States would supply 100 divisions of troops in August 1919, recruiting at least 300,000 people per month. In this way, the Allied powers could maintain their numerical superiority and achieve final victory.

Commander Pershing had a concrete expression of the Allied forces' appeal to the United States. On June 9, when the German 19th Army was advancing towards the Champagne region, the commander of the American Expeditionary Force came to Menin to see me, reiterating his meaning of March 28. He earnestly said to me that he was fully aligned with the Allied forces and that he eagerly wished for all of his troops to participate in the war. At the same time, he truly represented the unanimous public opinion of the United States. He said that the United States was determined to fully participate in the war, regardless of the cost.

This expression of public opinion was very beneficial to the military of the Allied governments. Unfortunately, material obstacles limited American cooperation. Unfortunately, these obstacles were very significant. On June 14, I submitted a memorandum to the Prime Minister, stating the importance of this point.

In the memorandum, I discussed the basis on which the plan for transporting American troops to France in the second half of 1918 should be established. While hoping for a large number of American troops to come to France, I pointed out the various reasons that could hinder its realization, such as ships, horses, and military equipment, etc., because there must be "careful preliminary research in all departments, as well as coordination between governments, to establish definite numbers."

With the permission of the Prime Minister, I proceeded to conduct research with Mr. Tideau and drafted a plan based on the following examples:

If the Allied forces want to be in a secure winning position in 1919, they must occupy a numerical advantage of more than 220 or 240 divisions of German troops, that is, 80 divisions of American troops must be sent by July 1919.

In order for the American troops to have three months of training before boarding the ship, the last unit arriving in April 1919 must be composed of soldiers recruited in December 1918. Each division must have 41,000 people. Therefore, at least 300,000 people must be recruited in the six months of the second half of 1918 and the four months of the first half of 1919.

This plan was approved by Commander Pershing at the Chemin Conference on June 23, submitted to the Versailles Supreme Military Council for approval on July 2, and then forwarded to President Wilson, who immediately replied that there could be 100 divisions of American troops by July 1, 1919, and if necessary, he would order other troops to be mobilized.

Ships were the main difficulty. First, because of the efforts of the American merchant ships (Note: By the end of the war, the American army used 3.8 million tons of ships, but only 94,000 tons when the American army began to participate in the war.), and second, because of the help of the British naval commander, this problem was gradually resolved.

Only the continuous increase of American troops (Note: By mid-June 1918, the American troops in the two places of the United States and Jiang had increased to 42 divisions, totaling 1,747,000 people.), Commander Pershing was even more eager to form independent troops. On July 10, he came to see me, requesting that the American troops in the French defense zone be formed into an independent army corps, and requesting the supply of artillery units, and if necessary, they would be transferred from the French army.

This time, I earnestly pleaded with Commander Pershing, saying that no one was more eager than I to form an independent American army corps, so that the American army could fight alone. I am doing my best for this matter. I firmly believe that soldiers of any country will only fight to the death under their own leaders and under their own flags, because this is related to the honor and disgrace of the nation itself. Unfortunately, the lack of artillery made the supply of American artillery units a problem, otherwise the independent American army corps could be formed.

The purpose of the Allied forces is to gain numerical superiority. If the French artillery units are withdrawn to make up for the shortage of the American army, it may not be beneficial to the Allied forces. On the contrary, if the American army has no artillery units, and if it is used in a quiet area to replace the French army, so that the French army can be transferred to help the war, it will be of great help.

The assistance of the American army is not limited to the Western Front.

On June 17, Commander Bliss came to Menin to see me for the matter of Marquis Milner requesting President Wilson to send 4,000 American troops to Murmansk and Arkhangelsk.

President Wilson was half cautious and half unwilling to reduce the number of American troops and transfer them to the French front, so he had no intention of accepting Marquis Milner's suggestion.

But six days later, I learned that the German army had withdrawn several divisions from the Russian border to France, so I also telegraphed President Wilson, saying that this fact could be regarded as "a powerful military basis for the Allied forces to urgently go to Siberia." On June 27, in the second telegram I sent to the American President, I re-emphasized this point and requested him to immediately order two regiments of American troops to be transferred to Siberia.

On July 2, this issue was raised when the Supreme Council met in Versailles, and the entire incident was studied by the leaders of the Allied governments.

In order to determine the organization and maintenance of each army under the Supreme Commander of the Allied forces, the authority of the Allied Marshal must be gradually expanded to reach the interior of the Allied countries and include the entire war zone. The format of the London Conference was thus expanded.

But while the battles were raging everywhere, the Western Front was still the decisive area. The Western Front, from the mouth of the Eisner River to the mouth of the Piave River, was vast and boundless, and all fell within its scope.

While the battle in France was important, the importance of the Italian theater could not be ignored, because the development of the battles on both sides of the Alps could cause repercussions to each other. The first step was that the Allied forces could not be frustrated in Italy, and the second step was to quickly give them the opportunity to win. The Abbeville Conference decided that I would be responsible for the military affairs of the Italian theater, and I took this as a guideline.

In mid-July 1918, the time when the two armies were evenly matched was approaching. If the enemy did not attack, the time for our army to launch a large-scale offensive would be ripe. If the enemy entered first, our army could take the opportunity to attack.

On July 9, I instructed Commander Petain that when the 10th Army took the offensive, it would launch another attack between the Marne River and Limay to boost its momentum. This offensive battle was commanded by Commander Peislair, with the French 5th Army attacking the eastern flank of the enemy.

On July 13, I informed the Commander-in-Chief of the French Army of the outline of this plan in a letter, at which time he was deploying the strength for the great battle.

The troops needed for the first battle—to contain the enemy's advance—were mostly on their way, and this force could still be increased. The second battle—the counterattack—in addition to its own benefits, could also become a very effective defense method. This battle required extremely rapid mobilization of all forces in order to be effective.

On the afternoon of July 14, I went to Commander Petain's headquarters again and immediately decided that the French army would counterattack the German attack in the Champagne area. The German attack seemed imminent.

The preparations for this counterattack had been studied for several weeks. It took almost four days for the teams transferred from the forward troops to gather and deploy. If these teams were withdrawn from the defense line, it would be very dangerous if they were attacked by the enemy at this time.

However, I still ordered the preparations to begin on July 14. On that day, because of the German attack in the Champagne area, there was a situation of imminent action, so I agreed with Commander Petain in Plorevin that the preparations for the counterattack would be completed on the 18th. The enemy's attack would be counterattacked immediately.

While our army was preparing, an unstable atmosphere arose at the meeting of the Supreme War Council held in Versailles on July 4. Late that day, as the afternoon meeting was about to end, Mr. Lloyd George proposed a motion in English, which was later recorded in the minutes of the meeting and accepted by Mr. Clemenceau in the name of the French government. The content of this motion was first to restore the Versailles Committee, and second to restore the right of the military representatives of this committee to supervise the Allied operations plan. As a result, the sole right of the Allied Commander-in-Chief to decide and plan everything and the freedom to implement it were completely canceled.

After this motion was translated into French, I learned its meaning. The seriousness of this motion did not seem to be noticed by the members of the council. So I went to Paris to see Mr. Clemenceau. I told him that I could not accept this motion and could not continue to command the Allied forces under the current situation. So we went back to Versailles together to find Mr. Lloyd George, who was preparing to have dinner with the representatives of the territory. We immediately began discussions with the British Prime Minister and re-drafted a draft, in which I retained the full power to decide on the operations plan and was only responsible to the heads of state. If the military representatives of each country wanted to make any suggestions regarding the command of the war, they had to obtain my consent in advance.

At this time, the enemy was preparing to proceed. On July 14, the French army launched an attack and captured 27 prisoners. Under interrogation, the prisoners confessed that the German army was preparing to attack on the night of the 14th and 15th, and that the shelling would begin ten minutes after midnight.

Our army's counterattack preparations and counterattack artillery fire began to move along the entire line of the Central Army before the German army opened fire. Our army took the initiative and bombarded with a large number of newly appearing cannons. The enemy was greatly shocked.

However, the enemy still carried out its original plan relentlessly. At the appointed hour, the enemy's artillery units opened fire. Between 4:15 AM and 5:30 AM, the German infantry launched an attack on our army along the entire 56-mile line between Teri and Messiqi. The only ones that did not move were the Limay salient. East of Limay, thanks to Commander Julayde's proper handling, the enemy was unable to advance. The enemy column was broken by our army's dense and accurate artillery fire and the sweeping of the machine guns scattered on the outpost line before it reached the main line of the French 4th Army. On that day, the German army made several hand-to-hand attacks to capture this defense line, but all failed.

West of Limay, our army was not very successful. On the front line of the 5th Army, the enemy advanced rapidly towards Ypone between the Marne River and the Ender River. The center of the 5th Army (the French 5th Regiment and the Italian 2nd Regiment) was repelled to the second line. At the same time, the enemy crossed the Marne River on both sides of Tourman, drove away the outposts on the south bank, and deployed a bridgehead line facing the Mary Combresey Saint Angnen line, which was defended by the left wing of the French 5th Army and the right wing of the 6th Army.

On the 15th, the reserves of each army and the divisions of the general reserve were almost all put into the fire line to meet the enemy. In the evening, Commander Petain had only one infantry division and one cavalry division left in the rear defense of the 4th Army, and only one division in the rear of the 5th Army.

In this way, although the German attack was stopped on the front line of our 4th Army, it had won a victory on the front line of the 5th Army and at the junction of the 5th and 6th Armies. Here, the enemy broke through our defense line and even crossed the Marne River in Tourman. This partial victory would become the prelude to the enemy taking advantage of the victory to shake the nearby defense line and prevent our army from implementing the counterattack plan. Our army still needed two days to prepare for the counterattack. Would the plan be changed as a result? This was the urgent question on July 15. Seeing that the enemy's strength was strong and its progress was rapid, our army had no room for hesitation.

The battlefield in the Champagne area was 25 miles long, and the enemy had failed. The German front line that crossed the Marne River in Tourman was 12 miles long. The two battlefields were 18 miles apart, separated by the important town of Limay and the neighboring town of Monteny, which were still held by our army. In the 24 hours that our army still needed to complete the counterattack preparations, the enemy could hardly hope to resolve the battle on the Marne River.

On the other hand, when our army was ready, it could launch a surprise attack from the Aisne River to the Marne River with a 25-mile long battle line, making the enemy's victory completely futile. The key to success or failure was that our army resolutely and resolutely based on the original plan and adhered to the preemptive strategy, and carried out a counterattack between the Aisne River and the Marne River. At the same time, it should be vigilant against dangers that could occur anytime and anywhere. This was the best policy for our army to fight.

I used all my energy to direct this military operation on the 15th.

Although the Commander-in-Chief of the French Army had the same belief as me, because he had closer contact with the actual battle, he was particularly concerned about the German advance towards Ypone on the south bank of the Marne River. He wanted to postpone the counterattack preparations in order to use the troops prepared for the counterattack to resist the current situation.

On my way to Mo Xi to meet with Commander-in-Chief Haig, I stopped at Commander Fuyue's headquarters in the Noa area and learned of this plan. I immediately notified the headquarters that this plan must be corrected and that the counterattack preparations must not be delayed.

But seeing the reasonable concerns of the Commander-in-Chief of the French Army, I asked Commander-in-Chief Haig to send two British divisions to the French front. In this way, the British troops on the French front, together with the two divisions that had been opened up, totaled four divisions. Commander-in-Chief Haig agreed, and the British 13th and 34th Divisions set off for the French front.

The two British divisions, originally belonging to the British 12th Corps, were transferred to Commander Petain to reinforce the front line of the Central Army and temporarily take the defensive. These two divisions disembarked and stationed in the Coias River area, listening to my dispatch, either to reinforce the French 10th or 6th Army to take the offensive, or to help the French 3rd Army take the defensive.

In this way, the urgent need for defense was remedied, and the preparations for our army's counterattack could proceed unimpeded, and the strength deployed for the counterattack was also increased. (To be continued)

Society News Submission Guidelines

(1) The text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas

(2) News about hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life, etc., is limited to emotional paintings about various social life in pictures

(3) Photos that are related to news such as seasonal, scenery, animals, plants, and people are qualified. Female figures in seasonal and landscape photography are especially welcome.
